    Feng Yin Tang (Zhongjing)
    Treats wind-heat seizures and convulsions due to fright.
    Equal parts of: Purple quartz, white quartz, cold water stone, gypsum, dried ginger, rhubarb, dragon teeth, oyster, licorice, talc
    Crush the above ingredients, use one sheng of water, decoct until reduced to one third. Take warm after meals; it will be effective.

    Huo Xue Tong Jing Tang (Dongyuan)
    Treats tightness and spasms of the hands, constipation, and a red hot face.

    Grind to the size of large mung beans, prepare as a single dose, with two large cups of water, decoct until reduced to one cup. Take warm at any time. Ensure warmth and rub the hands near fire in the room.

    Danggui Longdan Pill
    According to the "Health Treasure" (same below)
    Treats kidney water yin deficiency, accumulated wind-heat, sudden palpitations, muscle spasms, restlessness, blockage of the nutrients and defensive qi, dizziness, muscle twitching, fullness and discomfort in the chest, difficulty in swallowing, dry and heavy intestines and stomach, urinary obstruction, tightness in the tendons and veins, weakness in limbs, and diseases caused by dark wind.     • 1 tael of Angelica sinensis
    • 1 tael of gentian
    • 1 tael of Cape jasmine fruit
    • 1 tael of coptis
    • 1 tael of berberine
    • 1 tael of scutellaria
    • 5 qian of rhubarb
    • 5 qian of aloe
    • 5 qian of indigo
    • 2.5 qian of aromatic wood
    • 0.5 qian of musk (to be ground separately)

    Grind the above eleven ingredients into a powder and form into pills the size of a mung bean. Take twenty pills with ginger soup after meals.

    Ajuga Pill
    Treats cold and dampness causing cold pain in muscles and bones, limiting movement. Ingredients:

    • 3 qian of peeled and fresh Sichuan black cocoon
    • 3 qian of black morning glory head powder
    • 3 qian of salt soybean
    • 1 qian each of ground frankincense and myrrh

    Grind the above into a powder and mix well. Use a handful of fat green onions, wash off the soil, and mix with one liter of light vinegar, avoiding copper and iron. Boil with gentle fire; filter out half the green onion vinegar, and continue to simmer until it forms a paste that does not disperse when dropped in water. Combine the previous powdered ingredients into pills the size of a tung seed. Take ten to twenty pills with warm wine; slight diarrhea indicates recovery.[62p]

    Zuo Jing Wan treats various ailments of the bones and muscles, including lack of movement in the hands and feet, and inability to walk or exercise, provided there is no prior acupuncture injury to the muscles or veins. Four or five pills will certainly be effective. After taking, there may be a slight urination, which indicates efficacy.

    Ingredients:

    • One tael of Angelica sinensis
    • Wood beet seeds, shelled and ground separately
    • White resin, ground separately
    • Five spirit resin, three and a half taels each
    • Fresh Aconitum, skin and navel removed, three and a half taels
    • One hundred blister beetles, heads, feet, and wings removed, cooked with some vinegar

    Grind the ingredients into a powder, mix two separately ground ingredients evenly, and use peeled black beans, one pound of fresh ground flour, and vinegar to make a paste. Form pills the size of a chicken's head. Each time, take one pill, followed by grinding it down with wine.

    Ban Xia Decoction treats cholera and cramping, with persistent vomiting and diarrhea.

    Ingredients:

    • Ten taels of Poria
    • Ten taels of Atractylodes macrocephala
    • Ten taels of Baijiu wheat
    • Two and a half qian of licorice
    • One and a half qian of light cinnamon

    Grind the ingredients into powder, and for those who are thirsty, take three qian with cool water; for those not thirsty, take with warm water, as needed.

    Wuling San (same as Zhongjing) treats cholera and cramping, especially for those who desire to drink water.

    Ingredients:

    • Eighteen qian of Polyporus
    • Eighteen qian of Poria
    • Eighteen qian of fried Atractylodes macrocephala
    • Half a tael of cinnamon
    • One tael and six and a half qian of Alisma

    Grind the ingredients into a powder, and take three qian each time. After taking, drink plenty of hot water, and sweating will lead to recovery.[63p]

    Huang Qi Wine (from "Yi Xue Zheng Chuan"): Treats wind-cold-dampness obstruction, persistent numbness in the body, dry and itchy skin, cramping and tightening of sinews, slurred speech, and weakness in hands and feet.     Liang Jing Pill treats excessive heart fire and muscle and tendon spasms.

    White Tiger Pill (from "Ancient and Modern Medical Reference") treats blue veins. It is said: "White Tiger Pill, ancient lime, made by the Spirit of Grain to save from disaster. Ground into powder and sifted through water, rolled into pills and sun-dried."

    For use, take 1-2 small cups of wine each time, swallowing 50 pills. This medicine is effective against ailments caused by blue veins, helps accumulate Yin energy throughout the cosmos.

    Regarding the ancient lime, scrape off impurities to make powder, using water to wash it. Do not allow it to dry out too much during sun-drying; shape it into pills the size of Wutong seeds. Take 50 pills each time, adjusting the quantity based on weight and effects, with wine to wash it down.

    This remedy can smooth qi, disperse blood, transform phlegm, and eliminate stagnation. For initial signs of blue veins, headaches, nausea, abdominal or lumbar pain, or widespread pain without appetite, taking a dose will disperse the blood at once. For persistent blue veins after three to five days, a higher dose will work effectively.

    It also treats pain in the heart and abdomen, and issues related to women’s menstruation or discharge, whether due to emotional distress, chronic dysentery, or internal injuries where blood stagnates—taking this pill will have significant effects.[66p]

    Ying Xue Di Huang Wan treats muscle cramps; it is suitable to take during spring and summer.
    Ingredients:

    • Cooked Rehmannia (Shu Di Huang) 2.5 candareens
    • Viticis Fructus (Manjingzi) 2.5 candareens

    • Dried Lacquer (Gan Qi) roasted,
    • Larvae (Qing Can) roasted,
    • Aconite (Tian Xiong),

    • Alisma (Bi Xie),
    • Chinese Yam (Shan Yao),
    • Alisma (Ze Xie),
    • Achyranthes (Niu Xi) each 1 liang.

    Grind the above into fine powder, form pills the size of a chestnut. Take 50 pills with warm wine.

    Ling Yang Jiao Tang treats muscle cramps and joint pain; it is suitable to take in autumn.
    Ingredients:

    • Antelope Horn (Ling Yang Jiao),
    • Cinnamon (Rou Gui),
    • Aconite (Fu Zi),
    • Angelica (Du Huo) each 1 liang and 3.5 candareens
    • White Peony Root (Bai Shao),
    • Siler (Fang Feng),
    • Chuanxiong (Xiong) each 1 liang.

    Grind the above into coarse powder, take 5 candareens with 1.5 cups of water, add 3 slices of fresh ginger, simmer until reduced to 8 parts, take the clear juice. Can be taken 2 to 3 times a day.

    Wei Shen San treats muscle cramps.
    Ingredients:

    • Euphorbia (Gan Su) powder 3 candareens, mix with finely chopped wild boar kidney, marinate with a little salt and pepper, fill with the herbal powder, wrap in lotus leaf, and cook until done. Chew with warm wine.

    Antelope Horn Powder treats liver wind causing muscle spasms and limb pain.

    Ingredients:

    • Antelope horn shavings: 1 ounce
    • Honey-fried licorice: 0.5 ounce
    • Gardenia seeds: 0.5 ounce
    • Cimicifuga: 0.75 ounce
    • Saposhnikovia: 0.75 ounce
    • Sour jujube seeds: 0.75 ounce
    • White mulberry bark: 0.75 ounce
    • Notopterygium: 0.75 ounce

    Preparation: Grind the above ingredients, take 3 grams per dose, mixed with one medium cup of water, add five slices of fresh ginger, and decoct until reduced to two-thirds. Strain and take warm, without regard to time, avoiding hot foods like pork and garlic.

    Single Prescription

    For cramps in the abdomen: Take the dung of a butcher's child about the size of a chicken egg, mix with warm wine, and take; vomiting will indicate recovery. [Shizhen]

    For muscle knots on the body: Use a wooden spoon to hit three times to disperse them. [Zangqi]

    For muscle cramps in the legs: Liu Yuxi in "Continued Transmission of Trusting Recipes" recommends using half a pound of yellow wax, melting it, and applying it onto an old silk cloth. Depending on the size and severity of the affliction, while warm, wrap it around the foot, especially at the sole; cover with a sock, changing when cold; also apply to the palms. [Tujing]

    For cholera-related muscle cramps washing method: Use a handful of large lizardwort, decoct in water for washing, which takes effect immediately. [Medical Truth][73p]

    　　肝虚转筋：用赤蓼豆叶切作三合，水一盏，酒三合，煎至四合，去滓，温分二服。 【《圣惠方》】
    　　脚转筋，疼痛挛急：松节二两，细銼如米粒，乳香一钱，用银石器内慢火炒令焦，只留一分性，出火毒，研细，每服一钱至二钱，热木瓜酒调下，同是筋病皆治之。一方用松节一两。【孙用和《秘宝方》】

    Liver deficiency causing spasms: Use red smartweed leaves, cut into three segments, add one cup of water and three cups of wine, and simmer until reduced to four cups. Strain and divide into two doses to be taken warm.

    For spasms in the feet, causing pain and contraction: Take two taels of pine resin, finely ground like rice grains, and one penny of frankincense. Fry them slowly in a silver or stone vessel until charred, leaving only a little potency. Remove from heat, grind finely, and take one to two pennies with hot papaya wine. This treats all muscle ailments. Alternatively, use one tael of pine resin alone.

    For spasms: Take used cotton and soak it in strong vinegar, then steam it. While hot, wrap it around the patient's foot, replacing it when it cools. Do not pause until healed.

    To treat unbearable spasms throughout the body: Prepare an extremely salty soup and soak the afflicted area in it.

    Muscle relaxation method: For conditions after injuries where muscles contract and do not extend, this method can also be used for other muscle shrinkages. Use a bamboo tube longer than a foot, drill holes at both ends, tie a rope, and hang it around the waist. When seated, raise the legs to roll them. Do not count the time; it will prove effective over time. There was a person who fell from a horse and broke his leg; his foot muscles contracted and he couldn't walk. He met a man who taught him this method, and after several days, he recovered as usual.

    For wind-cold causing muscle and joint contraction: Bathe in a warm spring; those who are very damp should avoid it.[74p]

    Muscle Cramps: Steep sheep wool in vinegar and wrap around the foot.

    Strengthening the muscles and the elixir of immortality: Use one pound of bright pine resin, boil it several times in a sand pot with ash-free wine over a mulberry wood fire, stirring with bamboo sticks until thick, then stop the fire. Pour it into water to form lumps, then boil again with wine nine times, until the resin is like jade, not bitter or acrid. Grind into a fine powder, using twelve taels, mix with half a pound each of white tuckahoe powder, yellow chrysanthemum powder, and cypress seed after removing oil and frost. Form into pills the size of a walnut using honey, taking seventy-two pills on an empty stomach with good wine. One should select an auspicious day for preparation and ensure that no women or chickens see it.

    Another recipe: Songmei pills, made with pine resin, boil it three times with flowing water and mulberry wood, then use mulberry ash to extract the juice and boil seven times. Stretch and pull, then boil twice with good wine and twice more with flowing water until it turns white and is not bitter. For every pound, add ten taels of nine-steamed rehmannia powder and six taels of black plum powder. Form into pills the size of a walnut, taking seventy pills with salty rice soup on an empty stomach. This strengthens the yang, tonifies the center, enhances muscle strength, and greatly benefits the body.[79p]

    　　　　针灸

    　　《素问》曰：春刺秋分，筋挛逆气，环为咳嗽，病不愈，令人时惊，又且哭。　　病有在脉者，刺脉无伤筋，筋伤则内动肝，肝动则春病热而筋弛。　　刺筋无伤肉者，至肉而去，不及筋也。刺肉无伤筋者，过肉中筋也。此之谓反也。　　病在筋，筋挛节痛，不可以行，名曰筋痹。刺筋上为故，刺分肉间，不可中骨也。病起筋炅，病已止。　　《灵枢》曰：关刺者，直刺左右尽筋上，以取筋痹，慎勿出血，此肝之应也。或曰渊刺，一曰岂刺。　　恢刺者，直刺旁之，举之前后，恢筋急，以治筋痹也。　　手屈而不伸者其病在筋，伸而不屈者其病在骨。在骨守骨，在筋守筋。　　转筋于阳治其阳，转筋于阴治其阴，皆卒刺之。　　暴挛癎眩，足不任身，取天柱。[80p]

    Acupuncture

    The "Su Wen" states: In spring, acupuncture at autumn equinox can relieve muscle spasms and counteract adverse qi, which can cause coughing, and if the condition does not improve, it may lead to sudden fright and weeping. If the disease is in the vessels, acupuncture at the vessel will not injure the muscles; if the muscles are injured, it will affect the liver, and if the liver is affected, the spring illness will manifest as heat causing the muscles to relax. Acupuncture that targets the muscles will not injure the flesh, but when it reaches the flesh, it could affect the muscles. Acupuncture that targets the flesh without affecting the muscles will pass through and touch the muscles. This is known as reversal.

    When the disease is in the muscles, causing spasms and joint pain, it may prevent movement, and this is called muscle paralysis. Acupuncture should be done on the muscles above, and the treatment should not reach the bones. If the disease arises from muscle distension, and if the condition has ceased, it should be noted.

    The "Ling Shu" says: For joint acupuncture, the needle should be inserted directly on either side along the muscles to address muscle paralysis; caution should be taken to avoid bleeding, as this corresponds to the liver. Some refer to this as "Yuan acupuncture," or "Qi acupuncture."

    For "Hui acupuncture," the needle is inserted on the sides, lifting it forward and backward, to relieve muscle tension and treat muscle paralysis. If the arm is bent and cannot stretch, the issue lies in the muscles; if it stretches but cannot bend, the issue is in the bones. One should focus on preserving the bones with bone issues and the muscles with muscle issues.

    When dealing with muscle cramps in the yang, treat the yang; when handling muscle cramps in the yin, treat the yin—all of this requires precise acupuncture. For violent cramps, convulsions, and dizziness, if the feet cannot support the body, one should target the Tian Zhu point.[80p]

    　　筋癫疾者，身倦挛急，大刺项大经之大杼脉。呕多沃沫，气下泄，不治。　　热病，面青，脑痛，手足躁，取之筋间，以第四针于四逆。筋躄目浸，索筋于肝；不得，索之金，金者肺也。　　热病数惊，瘈瘲而狂，取之脉，以第四针急泻有余者。癫疾毛发去，索血于心；不得，索之水，水者肾也。　　厥心痛，与背相控，善瘲，如从后触其心，伛偻者，肾心痛也。先取京骨、昆仑；发针不已，取然谷。　　黄帝曰：人之亸者何气使然？岐伯曰：胃不实则诸脉虚，诸脉虚则筋脉懈惰，筋脉懈惰则行阴用力，气不能复，故为亸。因其所在，补分肉间。[81p]

    Those suffering from convulsive diseases exhibit weakness and tension; severe needling at the large spine and major vessels of the neck is necessary. They experience excessive vomiting of foamy fluid and downward gas release; if left untreated, it worsens.

    In cases of fevers, with a pale face, headaches, and restless limbs, needling between the tendons with the fourth needle at the four extremes is advised. For muscle atrophy and drowning vision, one must seek the tendons linked to the liver; if that fails, then those related to metal, which corresponds to the lungs.

    In fevers accompanied by frequent scares, leading to seizures and madness, the pulse should be taken, using the fourth needle to drain the excess. If convulsive diseases cause hair loss, blood should be sought from the heart; if that fails, look to water, which relates to the kidneys.

    For heart pain accompanied by back tension, and if there are sudden seizures as if the heart is being touched from behind, it indicates kidney-related heart pain. First, needle the Jinggu and Kunlun; if the needling doesn’t stop, then proceed to the Rangu point.

    The Yellow Emperor asked: What causes these ailments? Qi Bo replied: If the stomach is insufficient, all pulses become weak. If the pulses are weak, the tendons become lax; when the tendons are lax, the energy cannot restore itself, leading to ailments. Therefore, one should supplement the areas where weakness exists, nourishing the flesh in between.[81p]

    　　黄帝问于伯高曰：何以知筋之病也？伯高曰：目色青黄赤白黑者，病在筋。筋部无阴无阳，无左无右，候病所在。黄帝曰：取之奈何？伯高曰：百病变化，浮沉深浅，不可胜穷，各在其处。病间者浅之，甚者深之，间者少之，甚者众之，随变而调气，故曰上工。　　《甲乙经》云：卒心中痛，瘈瘲互相引，肘内廉痛，心敖敖然，间使主之。　　热病，先手臂瘈瘲，唇口纵，鼻张，目下汗出如转珠，两乳下二寸，坚胁满悸，列缺主之。　　振寒瘈瘲，手不伸，咳嗽唾浊，气膈善呕，尺泽主之。　　大风默默不知所痛，嗜卧善惊，瘈瘲，天井主之。　　头重鼻衄及瘈瘲，至阴主之。[82p]

    The Yellow Emperor asked Bo Gao: How do you know the diseases of the tendons? Bo Gao replied: The colors of the eyes—blue, yellow, red, white, and black—indicate illness in the tendons. The tendon area has neither yin nor yang, neither left nor right; it is important to observe where the illness is located. The Yellow Emperor asked: How can this be treated? Bo Gao said: Diseases change and manifest in various ways, sometimes floating, sometimes sinking, sometimes appearing shallow, and at other times deep; they cannot be fully exhausted in understanding, as each exists in its own place. For illnesses in between, treat them lightly; for those that are severe, treat them deeply; adjust the qi according to the changes, hence it is said to be skilled work.

    The "Classic of Changes" states: Sudden chest pain, spasms in succession, pain inside the elbow, a feeling of fullness in the heart, treat accordingly.

    For heat diseases, first accompanied by spasms in the arms, the lips and mouth open, the nose flares, sweating beneath the eyes like turning pearls, if pain is two inches below the breasts and the sides are hard and full with palpitation, treat using Lie Que.

    For chill with spasms, the hand cannot stretch, accompanied by a cough and thick phlegm, and a sensation of blockage with nausea, treat using Chi Ze.

    For great wind with silent pain, a tendency to sleep and be startled, and spasms, treat using Tian Jing.

    For heavy head, nosebleeds, and spasms, treat using Zhi Yin.[82p]

    　　身热狂走，讝语见鬼，瘈瘲，身柱主之。　　《难经》云：筋会阳陵泉，筋病治此。　　《千金方》云：腹满瘈瘲，心痛气满不得息，巨阙主之。　　呕血时瘈，善摇头，颜青，汗出不过肩，伤寒温病，曲泽主之。　　转筋十指挛急，不得屈伸，灸脚外踝骨上七壮。　　失精筋挛，阴缩入腹，相引痛，灸中封五十壮，在内踝前筋里宛宛中。　　又云：灸下满各五十壮，老人加之，小儿随年壮法。　　又云：此二穴喉肿厥逆，五脏所苦，鼓胀，悉以主之。　　转筋，胫骨痛不可忍，灸屈膝下廉横筋上三壮。　　腹胀转筋，灸脐上一寸，二七壮。[83p]

    When the body is hot and restless, and strange words make one feel like seeing ghosts, with symptoms of convulsions, the governing point is the spine. The "Nan Jing" states: the sinews meet at Yanglingquan; treat sinew diseases here. The "Qian Jin Fang" mentions: with abdominal fullness and convulsions, heart pain with gas fullness that cannot be exhaled, the major point is the abdomen. During vomiting blood accompanied by convulsions, shaking the head vigorously, turning blue in the face, and sweating less than the shoulders, treat with Quze for cold damage and warm diseases. For cramping of the fingers, unable to bend or stretch, moxibustion should be applied above the outer ankle bone with seven punctures. For loss of essence leading to muscle cramping and the genitals retracting into the abdomen, pulling pain; apply moxibustion with fifty punctures at the point slightly inside the inner ankle tendons. Additionally, moxibustion below each fullness with fifty punctures. For the elderly, increase the number, and for children, follow the growth with age. It is also noted: these two points address throat swelling and counterflow, afflictions of the five organs, and all kinds of distention. For cramps, with unbearable pain in the shinbone, perform moxibustion three times on the tendons above the knees. For abdominal distention and cramping, apply moxibustion one inch above the navel with twenty-seven punctures.[83p]

    　　劳冷气逆，腰髋冷痹，脚屈难伸，灸阳蹺一百壮，在外踝下，容爪。　　腰背不便转筋，急痹筋挛，灸第二十一椎，随年壮。　　《卫生宝鉴》曰：张仲文传神仙灸法，腰膝重痛，不可转侧，起坐难，及冷痹脚筋挛急，不可转侧屈伸，灸曲膝两文头左右脚四处，各三壮，每灸一脚，二火齐下，艾炷到肉，初觉疼痛，用二人两边齐吹，至火灭，午时着灸，人定已来，脏腑自动一两行，或转动如雷声，其疾立愈。此法神效，卒不可量也。　　尺泽去肘疼筋紧。尺泽，肺经，在肘约横纹中。　　《医学纲目》曰：筋挛骨痛，补魂门。　　膝曲筋急不能舒，取曲泉。[84p]

    Labor causes coldness to react, resulting in cold blockage in the waist and hips, making it difficult to stretch the legs. Apply moxibustion on the Yangqiao point with one hundred strong sessions, beneath the outer ankle, with a pinching motion. The waist and back are inconvenient to move due to muscle cramps, with urgent spasms. Perform moxibustion on the twenty-first vertebra, as needed based on individual strength.

    According to the "Treasure of Health," Zhang Zhongwen transmitted the method of divine moxibustion. For severe pain in the waist and knees, making it hard to turn or sit, and for cold blockages causing muscle spasms in the legs, one cannot turn or bend. Apply moxibustion on the two "wen" points at the back of the knee on both legs, three sessions each. For each leg, use two fires simultaneously, ensuring the moxa reaches the flesh. Initially, there will be pain; with two people blowing on either side until the fire goes out, perform this at noon when the person is calm. The internal organs will move a bit, or may rotate like thunder, leading to rapid recovery. This method is incredibly effective and cannot be measured.

    The point Xiezhe reduces pain and tightness near the elbow. Xiezhe is located on the lung meridian, at the horizontal line of the elbow crease. According to the "Medical Treatise," for muscle spasms and bone pain, nourish the Soul Gate. For a bent knee with tightness that cannot be released, use the Quxuan point.[84p]

    　　筋急不能行，内踝筋急，灸内踝四十壮；外踝筋急，灸外踝三十壮，立愈。　　膝筋挛急不开，两膝内外曲交尖，各灸二七壮，即委阳穴。　　转筋而痛，泻承山，或灸二七壮。
    　　肝热生筋痿，补行间，泻太冲。
    　　筋挛阴缩痛，灸中封五十壮。

    　　　　医案

    　　《儒门事亲》曰：黄如村一叟，两手搐搦，状如拽锯，冬月不能覆被，适戴人之舞阳，道经黄如，不及用药，针其两手大指后中注穴上。戴人曰：自肘已上皆无病，惟两手搐搦，左氏所谓风淫末疾者此也。或刺后溪，手太阳穴也，屈小指握纹尽处，是穴也。[85p]

    When the tendons are tight and cannot move, if the inner ankle tendons are tight, apply moxibustion with forty stalks to the inner ankle; if the outer ankle tendons are tight, apply moxibustion with thirty stalks to the outer ankle, and it will be instantly cured.

    If the knee tendons are cramping and cannot open, where the inner and outer curves of both knees intersect, apply moxibustion with twenty-seven stalks to each, at the Weiyang point.

    For cramping and pain, drain the Chengshan point, or apply moxibustion with twenty-seven stalks.

    Heat in the liver causes muscle atrophy; tonify the Xingjian point and drain the Taichong point.

    For cramping, tightening, and pain in the tendons, apply moxibustion with fifty stalks to the Zhongfeng point.

    Medical Case

    The "Rumen Shiqin" states: A man in Huangru Village, both hands trembled and twisted like a saw; he could not cover himself with a quilt in winter. While attending the dance of the person known as Dai, he passed through Huangru and did not have time to take medicine, so he needled the acupoint at the middle back of both thumbs. Dai said: "There is no illness above the elbow; the only problem is the trembling of both hands, which Left Master refers to as wind-induced minor ailments." Alternatively, one might needle the Houshu point; the hand Taiyang point; bend the little finger to the end of the line, that is the acupoint.[85p]

    　　《李杲十书》曰：灵寿县董监军，癸卯冬大雪时，因事到真定，勿觉有风气暴至，诊得六脉俱弦甚，按之洪实有力。其证手挛急，大便秘濇，面赤热，此风寒始至加于身也。四肢者，脾也。以风寒之邪伤之，则搐急而挛痹，乃风淫末疾而寒在外也。《内经》曰：寒则筋挛，正谓此也。本人素饮酒，内有实热，乘于肠胃之间，故大便秘濇而面赤热，内则手足阳明受邪，外则足太阴脾经受风寒之邪。用桂枝甘草以祛其寒邪，而缓其急搐；又以黄蘗之苦寒，以泻实而润燥，急救肾水；用升麻、葛根，以升阳气，行手足阳明之经，不令遏绝；更以桂枝辛热，入手阳明而润燥；复以芍药、甘草，专补脾气，使不受风寒之邪，而退木邪，专益肺金也；加人参以补元气，为之辅佐；加当归身，去里急而和血润燥，名活血通经汤。更令暖房中近火，摩搓其手，乃愈。
    　　《薛己医案》曰：一产妇筋挛臂软，肌肉抽掣，皆属气血虚，用十全大补汤而痊。[86p]

    The "Ten Books of Li Gao" states: In the winter of the Gui-Mao year, during heavy snowfall, Dong Jianjun from Ling Shou County, while attending to matters in Zhen Ding, unexpectedly experienced a sudden influx of wind. Upon examination, all six pulses were found to be tense, and a strong, wide pulse was present. The symptoms included hand spasms, constipation and dry stools, and a flushed, hot face, indicating the initial onset of wind-cold attacking the body. The limbs, corresponding to the spleen, were affected by the evil of wind-cold, resulting in spasms and rigidity as the wind troubled the minor ailments while the cold remained external. As stated in the "Inner Canon," cold causes the muscles to contract, which precisely describes this condition. The individual had a history of alcohol consumption, leading to internal heat accumulating in the digestive tract, causing constipation and a hot face. Internally, the Yangming channels in the hands and feet were influenced by the evil, while externally, the Taiyin spleen channel suffered from wind-cold. I used cinnamon twig and licorice to dispel the cold evil and alleviate the spasms; bitter and cold huanglian was employed to drain the excess and moisten dryness, providing urgent assistance to kidney water. I used sibia and kudzu root to elevate Yang energy, promoting the flow in the Yangming channels of the arms and legs, preventing stagnation. Additionally, cinnamon twig, being acrid and warm, entered the hand Yangming to moisten dryness; I added peony and licorice, specifically to replenish spleen energy, protecting against wind-cold and expelling wood malignancy, consequently benefiting lung metal. I included ginseng to replenish the primary energy for support; adding the body of angelica, I resolved internal urgency and harmonized the blood to moisten dryness, naming the formula "Active Blood Circulation Decoction." I further instructed the patient to stay in a warm room near the fire, rubbing her hands, leading to recovery.

    The "Medical Case of Xue Ji" states: A postpartum woman suffered from muscle spasms and soft arms, with her muscles twitching, all attributed to Qi and blood deficiency. She was treated with the "Shiquan Dabu Decoction" and recovered.[86p]

    　　一妇人素有痰火，忽然昏愦，瘈瘲抽搐，善惊数欠，四肢筋挛，痰涎上升，此肺金燥甚，血液衰少而然也。用清燥汤、六味丸兼服，寻愈。
    　　《寓意草》曰：徐岳生躯盛气充，昔年因食指微伤见血，以冷水濯之，遂至血凝不散，肿溃出脓血数升，小筋脱去三节，指废不伸。迩来两足间，才至秋月，便觉畏冷，重绵蔽之，外拊仍热，内揣独觉其寒。近日从踵至膝后筋痛，不便远行。云间老医令服八味丸，深中其意。及仆诊，自云，平素脉难摸索，乃肝肺二部反见洪大，大为病进。况在冬月，木落金寒时，尤为不宜。方来之势，将有不可向迩者，八味丸之桂、附，未可轻服。何也？筋者，肝之合也。附筋之血，既经食指之挹取，存留无几，不能荣养筋脉，加以忿怒数动，肝火传热于筋，足跗之大筋，得热而短，是以牵强不便于行也。然肝之所主者惟肺，木性畏金，禀令拥戴，若君主然，故必肺气先清，周身气乃下行。[87p]

    A woman who was usually affected by phlegm and heat suddenly became faint, experiencing spasms and convulsions, with frequent startles. Her limbs were stiff, and phlegm rose up. This was due to severe dryness in the lung and insufficient blood. She was treated with Qingzao Decoction and Liuwei Pill, and soon recovered.

    In the "Yuyi Grass" it is said: Xu Yue was robust, but years ago, after slightly injuring his finger and seeing blood, he washed it with cold water, which caused the blood to coagulate and not disperse. It swelled and produced several pints of pus and blood, and the tendons retracted, resulting in dysfunction of the finger. Recently, between his legs, he found himself feeling cold as autumn moon approached, heavily covering himself, feeling hot on the outside but cold within. Recently, he experienced pain in the tendons from heel to knee, making it inconvenient to travel far.

    An old doctor advised him to take Bawei Pill, deeply understanding its significance. Upon examining him, I found his pulse difficult to sense, but the pulses of the liver and lungs were notably strong, indicating a serious condition. Especially in winter, when wood falls and metal is cold, this is particularly unsuitable. The current condition may worsen if not addressed, and one should be cautious with the ingredients of Bawei Pill, especially the cinnamon and aconite.

    Why is this? The tendons are linked to the liver. The blood nourishing the tendons could hardly be available due to the previous finger injury, which cannot sustain them. Coupled with anger and frequent movements, liver heat transfers to the tendons, causing stiffness in the large tendons of the feet, leading to discomfort and difficulty in walking. However, the liver governs the lungs, and wood is fearful of metal; if the lungs do not clear, then the energy cannot circulate downward throughout the body.[87p]

    今肺脉大，则肺气又为心主所伤，壅窒不清，是以阳气不能下达而足寒也。然则所患虽微，已犯三逆。平素脉细，而今脉大，一逆也；肝脉大而热下传，二逆也；肺脉大而气上壅，三逆也。设误以桂、附治之，热者愈热，壅者愈壅，即日便成痿痹矣。此际用药，渊乎微乎，有寻常不能测识者。盖筋脉短劲，肝气内锢，须亟讲以金伐木荣之道，以金伐木，而木反荣，筋反舒，匪深通元造者，其孰能知之！然非金气自壅，则木且奉令不暇，何敢内拒？惟金失其刚，转而为柔，是以木失其柔，转而为刚，故治此患，先以清金为第一义也。然清金又先以清胃为第一义，不清其胃，则饮酒焉而热气输于肺矣，厚味焉而浊气输于肺矣。药力几何，能胜清金之任哉？金不清，如大敌在前，主将懦弱，已不能望其成功，况舍清金，而更加以助火铄金，倒行逆施以为治耶？必不得之数矣。
    [88p]

    When the lung pulse is large, the lung qi is harmed by the heart's dominion, resulting in obstruction and unclear flow; hence the yang qi cannot descend, leading to cold in the extremities. Although the ailment seems minor, it has already violated the three reversals. Normally, the pulse is fine, but now it is large: one reversal. The liver pulse is large and heat descends, presenting the second reversal. The lung pulse is large and the qi is obstructed upwards, representing the third reversal. If one mistakenly uses cinnamon or aconite to treat it, the heat will become hotter and the obstruction will worsen, leading to atrophy or paralysis within a day. At this juncture, when using medication, it is crucial to be subtle and discerning, as common understanding may not grasp it. The sinews and vessels are short and rigid, the liver qi is internally trapped; thus, one must urgently discuss the method of using metal to conquer wood. By using metal to conquer wood, wood will counter-vigorously thrive, and the sinews will relax. If one does not deeply understand the primordial creation, who can know this? If the metal qi is not obstructed, wood would hasten to fulfill its command without hesitation; how could it dare to resist inwardly? Only if the metal loses its rigidity and turns soft can the wood lose its softness and become rigid. Therefore, when treating this ailment, the foremost principle is to clear the metal. However, clearing the metal first requires clarifying the stomach. If the stomach is not clear, one drinks alcohol, causing heat to be transmitted to the lungs; or consumes rich flavors, resulting in turbid qi being transmitted to the lungs. What medicinal power could possibly fulfill the duty of clearing metal? If the metal is not cleared, it is like having a formidable enemy in front; the general is feeble and cannot expect success. How could one abandon the clearing of metal and instead further assist fire to melt metal, thereby acting in direct opposition to treatment? Such an outcome is bound to be futile.[88p]
